INSERT INTO `LIENVIDEO` VALUES(543, 'It don''t mean a thing', 'Duke Ellington', 'http://www.youtube.com/embed/qDQpZT3GhDg', '', 'Duke Ellington and his orchestra playing this awesome tune in 1943.\r\n\r\n"It Don''t Mean a Thing (If It Ain''t Got That Swing)" is a 1931 composition by Duke Ellington with lyrics by Irving Mills, now accepted as a jazz standard. The music was written and arranged by Ellington in August 1931 during intermissions at Chicago''s Lincoln Tavern and was first recorded by Ellington and his orchestra for Brunswick Records (Br 6265) on February 2, 1932. Ivie Anderson sang the vocal and trombonist Joe Nanton and alto saxophonist Johnny Hodges played the instrumental solos. The title was based on the oft stated credo of Ellington''s former trumpeter Bubber Miley, who was dying of tuberculosis. The song became famous, Ellington wrote, "as the expression of a sentiment which prevailed among jazz musicians at the time." Probably the first song to use the phrase "swing" in the title, it introduced the term into everyday language and presaged the Swing Era by three years. The Ellington band played the song continuously over the years and recorded it numerous times, most often with trumpeter Ray Nance as vocalist.', 1943, 2, 1, 1, '1940-1955', 0, 0, NULL, '2012-02-16 16:51:00');

INSERT INTO `LIENVIDEO` VALUES(634, 'Rock Baby Rock it', 'Divers', '//www.youtube.com/embed/YkydPpWxYXk', '', 'This 1957 rock n'' roll quickie is famous (or infamous) in cult movie circles for it''s low budget charm, combined with a rare authentic look at then contemporary youth culture.\r\n\r\nUnlike it''s more slightly higher budgeted Hollywood contemporaries from Columbia Pictures ("Don''t Knock The Rock"), or Warner Brothers ("Untamed Youth"), or even American International ("Shake, Rattle, And Rock"), "Rock Baby Rock It!" was independently produced in Dallas, Texas.\r\n\r\nInstead of big names such as Bill Haley, Chuck Berry, Eddie Cochran, or Little Richard, this gem featured local Texas talent in the way of blues singer Roscoe Gordon, vocal group the Five Stars, Everly Brothers sound-alikes The Belew Twins, Bill Haley-type combo The Cell Block Seven, and local Texas rockabilly legend, Johnny Carroll.\r\n\r\nWhat makes these fine performers all the more exciting to watch here is the fact that, for the most part, they''re performing their numbers live for the camera, and not lip synced.\r\n\r\nAlso of interest for retro fans is seeing real teenagers doing real teen dance styles on film, rather than the usual 30-something professionals doing Big Band-era lindy hop in most other (Hollywood) rock n'' roll exploitation quickies.\r\n\r\nLook for Kay Wheeler, president of the largest Elvis Presley fan club at the time, doing her rock n'' bop routine. According to Alanna Nash''s book "Baby Let''s Play House", Ms. Wheeler''s dancing actually influenced Elvis'' hip shaking on stage. Whether true or not, you can definitely see the Elvis style in her dance routine to Johnny Carroll''s "Sugar Baby."\r\n\r\nA true time-capsule of a particular place in a particular moment in time, "Rock, Baby Rock It!" is a must-see for any fan of rockabilly or retro youth culture.\r\n\r\nEnjoy it while you can, since this upload will be yanked in a few weeks to be replaced with a more "enhanced" version.', 1957, 2, 2, 1, '1956-1970', 0, 0, NULL, '2013-09-12 06:50:00');

Cette \r\n              pierre m’atteindrait moi-même car je suis bien certain \r\n              d’une chose : le besoin de consolation que connaît l’être \r\n              humain est impossible à rassasier. \r\n            <p>\r\n              En ce qui me concerne, je traque la consolation comme le chasseur \r\n              traque le gibier. Partout où je crois l’apercevoir \r\n              dans la forêt, je tire. Souvent je n’atteins que le \r\n              vide mais, une fois de temps en temps, une proie tombe à \r\n              mes pieds. Et, comme je sais que la consolation ne dure que le temps \r\n              d’un souffle de vent dans la cime d’un arbre, je me \r\n              dépêche de m’emparer de ma victime.\r\n            <p>Qu’ai-je alors entre mes bras ?\r\n              <p>\r\n              Puisque je suis solitaire : une femme aimée ou un compagnon \r\n              de voyage malheureux. Puisque \r\n              je suis menacé par la mer : un récif de granit bien \r\n              dur.\r\n              <p>\r\n              Mais il y a aussi des consolations qui viennent à moi sans \r\n              y être conviées et qui remplissent ma chambre de chuchotements \r\n              odieux : Je suis ton plaisir – aime-les tous ! Je suis ta solitude – méprise les hommes \r\n              ! Je suis ton aspiration à la mort – alors tranche \r\n              !\r\n              <p>\r\n              Le fil du rasoir est bien étroit.
